margin-left: 1em; font-size:90%;">\n<li value="1">Of mixed <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">Genoese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maltese_people" title="Maltese people">Maltese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Special_Member_State_territories_and_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Special Member State territories and the European Union">Special Member State territory</a> of the United Kingdom.</li><li value="3">Coins and sterling notes are issued by the Government of Gibraltar.</li><li value="4">Unlike all other UK dependencies except the <a href="/wiki/British_Indian_Ocean_Territory" title="British Indian Ocean Territory">British Indian Ocean Territory</a>, since 16 June 1929.</li><li value="5">9567 from Spain before 10 February 2007.</li><li value="6">The <a href="/wiki/.eu" title=".eu">.eu</a> domain is also used, shared with other <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> member states. <big><br /><br /><a href="/wiki/Postcodes_in_the_United_Kingdom#Overseas_territories" title="Postcodes in the United Kingdom">UK Postcode:</a> GX11 1AA</big><sup id="cite_ref-gx111aa_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gx111aa-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup></li>\n</ol></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Gibraltar</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/d\xca\x92/: &#39;j&#39; in &#39;jam&#39;">d\xca\x92</span><span title="/\xc9\xaa/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">\xc9\xaa</span><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span><span title="/\xc9\x94\xcb\x90/: &#39;au&#39; in &#39;fraud&#39;">\xc9\x94\xcb\x90</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span><span title="/\xc9\x99r/: &#39;er&#39; in &#39;letter&#39;">\xc9\x99r</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <small>Spanish pronunciation:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[xi\xce\xb2\xc9\xbeal\xcb\x88ta\xc9\xbe]</a></span>) is a <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territories" title="British Overseas Territories">British Overseas Territory</a> located at the southern tip of the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> It has an area of 6.7&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (2.6&#160;sq&#160;mi) and is <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar%E2%80%93Spain_border" title="Gibraltar\xe2\x80\x93Spain border">bordered to the north</a> by Spain. The landscape is dominated by the <a href="/wiki/Rock_of_Gibraltar" title="Rock of Gibraltar">Rock of Gibraltar</a> at the foot of which is a densely populated city area, home to over 30,000 people, primarily <a href="/wiki/Gibraltarian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Gibraltarian people">Gibraltarians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> It shares a maritime border with <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>. Under the <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Constitution_Order_2006" title="Gibraltar Constitution Order 2006">Gibraltar constitution of 2006</a>, Gibraltar has limited powers of self-government, with some responsibilities, such as defence and foreign relations, remaining with the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Government of the United Kingdom">British government</a>.\n</p><p>In 1704, Anglo-Dutch forces <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_Gibraltar" title="Capture of Gibraltar">captured Gibraltar</a> from <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> during the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Spanish_Succession" title="War of the Spanish Succession">War of the Spanish Succession</a> on behalf of the <a href="/wiki/Habsburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Habsburg">Habsburg</a> claim to the Spanish throne. The territory was ceded to <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Great Britain</a> in perpetuity under the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Utrecht" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Utrecht">Treaty of Utrecht</a> in 1713. During World War II it was an important base for the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> as it controlled the entrance and exit to the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">Mediterranean Sea</a>, which is only 8 miles (13&#160;km) wide at this naval "<a href="/wiki/Choke_point" title="Choke point">choke point</a>". It remains strategically important, with half the world\'s seaborne trade passing through the strait.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Today Gibraltar\'s economy is based largely on tourism, online gambling, financial services and cargo ship refuelling.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Maec_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Maec-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-theguardian.com_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theguardian.com-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The sovereignty of Gibraltar is a point of contention in <a href="/wiki/Spain%E2%80%93United_Kingdom_relations" title="Spain\xe2\x80\x93United Kingdom relations">Anglo-Spanish relations</a> because Spain asserts <a href="/wiki/Disputed_status_of_Gibraltar" title="Disputed status of Gibraltar">a claim to the territory</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Maec_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Maec-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Gibraltarians rejected proposals for Spanish sovereignty in a <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_sovereignty_referendum,_1967" title="Gibraltar sovereignty referendum, 1967">1967 referendum</a> and, in a <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_sovereignty_referendum,_2002" title="Gibraltar sovereignty referendum, 2002">2002 referendum</a>, the idea of shared sovereignty was also rejected.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Gibraltar" title="History of Gibraltar">History of Gibraltar</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Moorish_Castle.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/The_Moorish_Castle.jpg/170px-The_Moorish_Castle.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/The_Moorish_Castle.jpg/255px-The_Moorish_Castle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/The_Moorish_Castle.jpg/340px-The_Moorish_Castle.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2136" data-file-height="2848" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Moorish_Castle.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View of the northern face of the <a href="/wiki/Moorish_Castle" title="Moorish Castle">Moorish Castle</a>\'s Tower of Homage</div></div></div>\n<p>Gibraltar was known as <i><a href="/wiki/Mons_Calpe" class="mw-redirect" title="Mons Calpe">Mons Calpe</a></i>, a name of Phoenician origin and one of the <a href="/wiki/Pillars_of_Hercules" title="Pillars of Hercules">Pillars of Hercules</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hills-13_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hills-13-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">Phoenicians</a> inhabited Gibraltar around 950 BC. Subsequently, Gibraltar became known as one of the <a href="/wiki/Pillars_of_Hercules" title="Pillars of Hercules">Pillars of Hercules</a>, after the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Greek</a> legend of the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">Strait of Gibraltar</a> by <a href="/wiki/Heracles" title="Heracles">Heracles</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Carthage" title="Carthage">Carthaginians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Romans</a> also established semi-permanent settlements. After the collapse of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire" title="Western Roman Empire">Western Roman Empire</a>, Gibraltar came briefly under the control of the <a href="/wiki/Vandals" title="Vandals">Vandals</a>, who crossed into Africa at the invitation of <a href="/wiki/Bonifacius" title="Bonifacius">Boniface</a>, the Count (or commander) of the territory. In prehistory evidence of <a href="/wiki/Neanderthal" title="Neanderthal">Neanderthal</a> habitation in Gibraltar has been discovered at <a href="/wiki/Gorham%27s_Cave" title="Gorham&#39;s Cave">Gorham\'s Cave</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The area later formed part of the <a href="/wiki/Visigothic_Kingdom" title="Visigothic Kingdom">Visigothic Kingdom</a> of <a href="/wiki/Hispania" title="Hispania">Hispania</a> from 414 AD until the <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_conquest_of_Hispania" title="Umayyad conquest of Hispania">Islamic conquest of Iberia</a> in 711 AD.\n</p><p>The name "Gibraltar" is the&#160;Spanish derivation of the&#160;Arabic&#160;name&#160;Jabal \xe1\xb9\xac\xc4\x81riq&#160;(\xd8\xac\xd8\xa8\xd9\x84 \xd8\xb7\xd8\xa7\xd8\xb1\xd9\x82), meaning "mountain of \xe1\xb9\xac\xc4\x81riq", which is named after <a href="/wiki/Tariq_ibn_Ziyad" title="Tariq ibn Ziyad">Tariq ibn Ziyad</a> &#160;(Arabic:&#160;\xd8\xb7\xd8\xa7\xd8\xb1\xd9\x82 \xd8\xa8\xd9\x86 \xd8\xb2\xd9\x8a\xd8\xa7\xd8\xaf) a&#160;Muslim&#160;commander who led the Islamic&#160;Umayyad&#160;conquest of&#160;Visigothic&#160;Hispania&#160;in 711\xe2\x80\x93718 A.D.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Settlement">Settlement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Settlement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 1160, the <a href="/wiki/Almohad_Caliphate" title="Almohad Caliphate">Almohad</a> Sultan <a href="/wiki/Abd_al-Mu%27min" title="Abd al-Mu&#39;min">Abd al-Mu\'min</a> ordered that a permanent settlement, including a castle, be built. It received the name of Medinat al-Fath (City of the Victory).<sup id="cite_ref-norris_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-norris-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> On completion of the works in the town, the Sultan crossed the Strait to look at the works and stayed in Gibraltar for two months. The Tower of Homage of the <a href="/wiki/Moorish_Castle" title="Moorish Castle">Moorish Castle</a> remains standing today. From 1274 onwards, the town was fought over and captured by the <a href="/wiki/Nasrid_dynasty" title="Nasrid dynasty">Nasrids</a> of Granada (in 1237 and 1374), the <a href="/wiki/Marinids" class="mw-redirect" title="Marinids">Marinids</a> of Morocco (in 1274 and 1333) and the kings of <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">Castile</a> (in 1309). In 1462, Gibraltar was finally captured by <a href="/wiki/Juan_Alonso_de_Guzm%C3%A1n,_1st_Duke_of_Medina_Sidonia" title="Juan Alonso de Guzm\xc3\xa1n, 1st Duke of Medina Sidonia">Juan Alonso de Guzm\xc3\xa1n, 1st Duke of Medina Sidonia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the conquest, <a href="/wiki/Henry_IV_of_Castile" title="Henry IV of Castile">Henry IV of Castile</a> assumed the additional title of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Gibraltar" title="Kingdom of Gibraltar">King of Gibraltar</a>, establishing it as part of the <i><a href="/wiki/Comarca" title="Comarca">comarca</a></i> of the <a href="/wiki/Campo_de_Gibraltar" title="Campo de Gibraltar">Campo Llano de Gibraltar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Six years later, Gibraltar was restored to the Duke of Medina Sidonia, who sold it in 1474 to a group of 4350 <i><a href="/wiki/Converso" title="Converso">conversos</a></i> (Christian converts from Judaism) from <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B3rdoba,_Spain" title="C\xc3\xb3rdoba, Spain">Cordova</a> and <a href="/wiki/Seville,_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Seville, Spain">Seville</a> and in exchange for maintaining the garrison of the town for two years, after which time they were expelled, returning to their home towns or moving on to other parts of Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> In 1501, Gibraltar passed back to the Spanish Crown, and <a href="/wiki/Isabella_I_of_Castile" title="Isabella I of Castile">Isabella I of Castile</a> issued a <a href="/wiki/Royal_warrant_(document)" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal warrant (document)">Royal Warrant</a> granting Gibraltar the coat of arms that it still uses today.\n</p><p>In 1704, during the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Spanish_Succession" title="War of the Spanish Succession">War of the Spanish Succession</a>, a combined <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">Anglo</a>-<a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Dutch</a> fleet, representing the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Alliance_(League_of_Augsburg)" title="Grand Alliance (League of Augsburg)">Grand Alliance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_Gibraltar" title="Capture of Gibraltar">captured the town of Gibraltar</a> on behalf of the <a href="/wiki/Charles_VI,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles VI, Holy Roman Emperor">Archduke Charles of Austria</a> in his campaign to become King of Spain. The occupation of the town by Alliance forces caused the exodus of the population to the surrounding area of the Campo de Gibraltar.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> As the Alliance\'s campaign faltered, the 1713 <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Utrecht" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Utrecht">Treaty of Utrecht</a> was negotiated and ceded control of Gibraltar to Britain to secure Britain\'s withdrawal from the war. Unsuccessful attempts by Spanish monarchs to regain Gibraltar were made with the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Gibraltar_(1727)" class="mw-redirect" title="Siege of Gibraltar (1727)">siege of 1727</a> and again with the <a href="/wiki/Great_Siege_of_Gibraltar" title="Great Siege of Gibraltar">Great Siege of Gibraltar</a> (1779 to 1783), during the <a href="/wiki/American_War_of_Independence" class="mw-redirect" title="American War of Independence">American War of Independence</a>.\n</p><p>Gibraltar became a key base for the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> and played an important role prior to the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Trafalgar" title="Battle of Trafalgar">Battle of Trafalgar</a> (21 October 1805) and during the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_War" title="Crimean War">Crimean War</a> of 1854\xe2\x80\x9356, because of its strategic location. Its strategic value increased with the opening of the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a>, as it lay on the sea route between the UK and the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> east of Suez. In the later 19th century, there were major investments in improving the fortifications and the port.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Modern_history">Modern history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Modern history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Military_history_of_Gibraltar_during_World_War_II" title="Military history of Gibraltar during World War II">Military history of Gibraltar during World War II</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Douglas_DC-3_of_BOAC_at_Gibraltar,_silhouetted_by_searchlights_on_the_Rock.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Douglas_DC-3_of_BOAC_at_Gibraltar%2C_silhouetted_by_searchlights_on_the_Rock.jpg/220px-Douglas_DC-3_of_BOAC_at_Gibraltar%2C_silhouetted_by_searchlights_on_the_Rock.jpg" width="220" height="219" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Douglas_DC-3_of_BOAC_at_Gibraltar%2C_silhouetted_by_searchlights_on_the_Rock.jpg/330px-Douglas_DC-3_of_BOAC_at_Gibraltar%2C_silhouetted_by_searchlights_on_the_Rock.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Douglas_DC-3_of_BOAC_at_Gibraltar%2C_silhouetted_by_searchlights_on_the_Rock.jpg/440px-Douglas_DC-3_of_BOAC_at_Gibraltar%2C_silhouetted_by_searchlights_on_the_Rock.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2486" data-file-height="2480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Douglas_DC-3_of_BOAC_at_Gibraltar,_silhouetted_by_searchlights_on_the_Rock.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Shown here during the Second World War, a <a href="/wiki/Douglas_Dakota" class="mw-redirect" title="Douglas Dakota">Douglas Dakota</a> of <a href="/wiki/BOAC" class="mw-redirect" title="BOAC">BOAC</a> is silhouetted at Gibraltar by the batteries of searchlights on the Rock, as crews prepare it for a night flight to the United Kingdom.</div></div></div><p>During the <a href="/wiki/Military_history_of_Gibraltar_during_World_War_II" title="Military history of Gibraltar during World War II">Second World War</a>, Gibraltar\'s civilian population was evacuated (mainly to London, but also to parts of <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> and <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a> and to <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Camp" class="mw-redirect" title="Gibraltar Camp">Gibraltar Camp</a> in <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>, and the Rock was strengthened as a <a href="/wiki/Fortification" title="Fortification">fortress</a>. The naval base and the ships based there played a key role in the provisioning and supply of the island of <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a> during <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Malta_(World_War_II)" title="Siege of Malta (World War II)">its long siege</a>. As well as frequent short runs (known as \'Club Runs\') towards <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a> to fly off aircraft reinforcements (initially <a href="/wiki/Hawker_hurricane" class="mw-redirect" title="Hawker hurricane">Hurricanes</a> but later, notably from the USN aircraft carrier <a href="/wiki/USS_Wasp_(CV-7)" title="USS Wasp (CV-7)">Wasp</a>, <a href="/wiki/Supermarine_Spitfire" title="Supermarine Spitfire">Spitfires</a>), the critical <a href="/wiki/Operation_Pedestal" title="Operation Pedestal">Operation Pedestal</a> convoy was run from Gibraltar in August 1942. This resupplied the island at a critical time in the face of concentrated air attacks from German and Italian forces. Spanish dictator <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">Francisco Franco</a>\'s reluctance to allow the <a href="/wiki/Wehrmacht" title="Wehrmacht">German Army</a> onto Spanish soil frustrated a German plan to capture the Rock, codenamed <a href="/wiki/Operation_Felix" title="Operation Felix">Operation Felix</a>.\n</p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_Naval_dockyard_and_South_Mole.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Gibraltar_Naval_dockyard_and_South_Mole.JPG/250px-Gibraltar_Naval_dockyard_and_South_Mole.JPG" width="250" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Gibraltar_Naval_dockyard_and_South_Mole.JPG/375px-Gibraltar_Naval_dockyard_and_South_Mole.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Gibraltar_Naval_dockyard_and_South_Mole.JPG/500px-Gibraltar_Naval_dockyard_and_South_Mole.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_Naval_dockyard_and_South_Mole.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Buildings of the former <a href="/wiki/HM_Dockyard,_Gibraltar" class="mw-redirect" title="HM Dockyard, Gibraltar">HM Dockyard, Gibraltar</a>, dating from the 1895 expansion</div></div></div>\n<p>In the 1950s, Franco renewed Spain\'s claim to sovereignty over Gibraltar and restricted movement between Gibraltar and Spain. Gibraltarians voted overwhelmingly to remain under British sovereignty in the <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_sovereignty_referendum,_1967" title="Gibraltar sovereignty referendum, 1967">Gibraltar sovereignty referendum, 1967</a>, which led to the passing of the <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Constitution_Order_1969" title="Gibraltar Constitution Order 1969">Gibraltar Constitution Order</a> in 1969. In response, Spain completely closed the border with Gibraltar and severed all communication links.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The border with Spain was partially reopened in 1982 and fully reopened in 1985 before Spain\'s accession to the <a href="/wiki/European_Community" class="mw-redirect" title="European Community">European Community</a>.\n</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_sovereignty_referendum,_2002" title="Gibraltar sovereignty referendum, 2002">a referendum held in 2002</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gibraltarian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Gibraltarian people">Gibraltarians</a> rejected by an overwhelming majority (98%) a proposal of shared sovereignty on which <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">Britain</a> were said to have reached "broad agreement".<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> The British government has committed itself to respecting the Gibraltarians\' wishes.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Constitution_Order_2006" title="Gibraltar Constitution Order 2006">new Constitution Order</a> was approved in referendum in 2006. A process of tripartite negotiations started in 2006 between Spain, Gibraltar and the UK, ending some restrictions and dealing with disputes in some specific areas such as air movements, customs procedures, telecommunications, pensions and cultural exchange.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/British_referendum_on_membership_of_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="British referendum on membership of the European Union">British referendum on membership of the European Union</a> 96% of <a href="/wiki/Gibraltarians_voted_to_remain" class="mw-redirect" title="Gibraltarians voted to remain">Gibraltarians voted to remain</a> on an 82% turnout.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Spain renewed calls for joint Spanish\xe2\x80\x93British control of the peninsula;<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> these were strongly rebuffed by Gibraltar\'s Chief Minister.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> On October 18, 2018, however, Spain agreed to abandon its objections to Gibraltar leaving the EU with Britain, with Spanish Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Pedro_S%C3%A1nchez_(politician)" title="Pedro S\xc3\xa1nchez (politician)">Pedro Sanchez</a> stating, \xe2\x80\x9cGibraltar will no longer be a problem in arriving at a Brexit deal.\xe2\x80\x9d<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Gibraltar" title="Politics of Gibraltar">Politics of Gibraltar</a></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Disputed_status_of_Gibraltar" title="Disputed status of Gibraltar">Disputed status of Gibraltar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Political_development_in_modern_Gibraltar" title="Political development in modern Gibraltar">Political development in modern Gibraltar</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_convent_in_Gibraltar_7.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/The_convent_in_Gibraltar_7.jpg/220px-The_convent_in_Gibraltar_7.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/The_convent_in_Gibraltar_7.jpg/330px-The_convent_in_Gibraltar_7.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/The_convent_in_Gibraltar_7.jpg/440px-The_convent_in_Gibraltar_7.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4752" data-file-height="3168" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_convent_in_Gibraltar_7.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Main Street entrance to the Governor\'s Residence, <a href="/wiki/The_Convent_(Gibraltar)" title="The Convent (Gibraltar)">The Convent</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_Parliament_at_dusk.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Gibraltar_Parliament_at_dusk.jpg/220px-Gibraltar_Parliament_at_dusk.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Gibraltar_Parliament_at_dusk.jpg/330px-Gibraltar_Parliament_at_dusk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Gibraltar_Parliament_at_dusk.jpg/440px-Gibraltar_Parliament_at_dusk.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_Parliament_at_dusk.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/John_Mackintosh_Square" title="John Mackintosh Square">John Mackintosh Square</a> entrance to the <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Parliament" title="Gibraltar Parliament">Gibraltar Parliament</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Under its current <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Constitution_Order_2006" title="Gibraltar Constitution Order 2006">constitution</a>, Gibraltar has almost complete internal <a href="/wiki/Self-governance" title="Self-governance">self-governance</a> through a <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Parliament" title="Gibraltar Parliament">parliament</a><sup id="cite_ref-publications.parliament.uk_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-publications.parliament.uk-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> elected for a term of up to four years. The <a href="/wiki/Unicameralism" title="Unicameralism">unicameral</a> parliament presently consists of 17 elected members, and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Speakers_of_the_Gibraltar_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Speakers of the Gibraltar Parliament">Speaker</a> who is not elected, but appointed by a resolution of the parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Gibraltar" title="Government of Gibraltar">government</a> consists of 10 elected members. The head of state is the British monarch, currently <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a>, who is represented by the <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Gibraltar" title="Governor of Gibraltar">Governor of Gibraltar</a>. The governor enacts day-to-day matters on the advice of the Gibraltar Parliament, but is responsible to the British government in respect of defence, foreign policy, internal security and general good governance.\nJudicial and other appointments are made on behalf of the monarch in consultation with the <a href="/wiki/Chief_Minister_of_Gibraltar" title="Chief Minister of Gibraltar">head of the elected government</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-news.bbc.co.uk_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-news.bbc.co.uk-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_general_election,_2011" title="Gibraltar general election, 2011">2011 election</a> was contested by the <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Social_Democrats" title="Gibraltar Social Democrats">Gibraltar Social Democrats</a> (GSD), <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Socialist_Labour_Party" title="Gibraltar Socialist Labour Party">Gibraltar Socialist Labour Party</a> (GSLP)-<a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Liberal_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="Gibraltar Liberal Party">Gibraltar Liberal Party</a> (GLP) Alliance and the <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Democratic_Party_(Gibraltar)" title="Progressive Democratic Party (Gibraltar)">Progressive Democratic Party</a> (PDP). The PDP was a new party, formed in 2006 and fielded candidates in the 2007 election, but none were elected. The head of government is the <a href="/wiki/Chief_Minister_of_Gibraltar" title="Chief Minister of Gibraltar">Chief Minister</a> (as of December 2011, <a href="/wiki/Fabian_Picardo" title="Fabian Picardo">Fabian Picardo</a>). All local political parties oppose any transfer of sovereignty to Spain, instead supporting <a href="/wiki/Self-determination" title="Self-determination">self-determination</a>. The main UK opposition parties also support this policy, and it is British government policy not to engage in talks about the sovereignty of Gibraltar without the consent of the people of Gibraltar.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Gibraltar is part of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, having joined through the <a href="/wiki/European_Communities_Act_1972_(UK)" title="European Communities Act 1972 (UK)">European Communities Act 1972 (UK)</a>, which gave effect to the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Accession_1972" title="Treaty of Accession 1972">Treaty of Accession 1972</a>, as a dependent territory of the United Kingdom under what was then article 227(4) of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_Establishing_the_European_Community" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty Establishing the European Community">Treaty Establishing the European Community</a> covering <a href="/wiki/Special_member_state_territories_and_the_European_Union#Gibraltar" title="Special member state territories and the European Union">special member state territories</a>, with exemption from some areas such as the <a href="/wiki/European_Union_Customs_Union" title="European Union Customs Union">European Union Customs Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Common_Agricultural_Policy" title="Common Agricultural Policy">Common Agricultural Policy</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a>. It is the only <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territory" class="mw-redirect" title="British Overseas Territory">British Overseas Territory</a> which is part of the European Union. After a 10-year campaign for the right to vote in <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Elections in the European Union">European elections</a>, since 2004 the people of Gibraltar have participated in elections for the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/South_West_England_(European_Parliament_constituency)" title="South West England (European Parliament constituency)">South West England constituency</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> On 23 June 2016 Gibraltar voted along with the United Kingdom in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum,_2016" title="United Kingdom European Union membership referendum, 2016">EU referendum</a>; 96% of its population voted to remain, but the overall United Kingdom result gave a 51.9% majority to leaving the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>  Nevertheless, Spanish President Pedro Sanchez stated on 18 October 2018 that the Gibraltar protocol had been "resolved" and that Spain will hold no objection when Gibraltar leaves the EU with Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Gibraltar was nominated to be included on the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_list_of_Non-Self-Governing_Territories" title="United Nations list of Non-Self-Governing Territories">United Nations list of Non-Self-Governing Territories</a> by the United Kingdom when the list was created in 1946<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> and has been listed ever since.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> The government of Gibraltar has actively worked to have Gibraltar removed from the list,<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> and in 2008 the British government declared Gibraltar\'s continued presence on the list an anachronism.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Gibraltar is not a member of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a> but was granted Associate Membership of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Foundation" title="Commonwealth Foundation">Commonwealth Foundation</a> in 2004. Gibraltar has competed in the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games" title="Commonwealth Games">Commonwealth Games</a> since 1958.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable mw-collapsible mw-collapsed">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="2">Party\n</th>\n<th colspan="2"><a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Parliament" title="Gibraltar Parliament">Members of Parliament</a>\n</th>\n<th colspan="6">6\n</th></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Rock_of_Gibraltar" title="Rock of Gibraltar">Rock of Gibraltar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Gibraltar" title="Bay of Gibraltar">Bay of Gibraltar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">Strait of Gibraltar</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Artificial_Reef" title="Gibraltar Artificial Reef">Gibraltar Artificial Reef</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rock_of_Gibraltar_from_the_Mediterranean_Steps.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Rock_of_Gibraltar_from_the_Mediterranean_Steps.jpg/220px-Rock_of_Gibraltar_from_the_Mediterranean_Steps.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Rock_of_Gibraltar_from_the_Mediterranean_Steps.jpg/330px-Rock_of_Gibraltar_from_the_Mediterranean_Steps.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Rock_of_Gibraltar_from_the_Mediterranean_Steps.jpg/440px-Rock_of_Gibraltar_from_the_Mediterranean_Steps.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rock_of_Gibraltar_from_the_Mediterranean_Steps.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View of the Rock of Gibraltar from the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Steps" title="Mediterranean Steps">Mediterranean Steps</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_aerial_view_looking_northwest.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Gibraltar_aerial_view_looking_northwest.jpg/220px-Gibraltar_aerial_view_looking_northwest.jpg" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Gibraltar_aerial_view_looking_northwest.jpg/330px-Gibraltar_aerial_view_looking_northwest.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Gibraltar_aerial_view_looking_northwest.jpg/440px-Gibraltar_aerial_view_looking_northwest.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="819" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_aerial_view_looking_northwest.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Gibraltar from the air, looking north-west</div></div></div>\n<p>Gibraltar\'s territory covers 6.7 square kilometres (2.6&#160;sq&#160;mi) and shares a 1.2-kilometre (0.75&#160;mi) land border with Spain. The town of <a href="/wiki/La_L%C3%ADnea_de_la_Concepci%C3%B3n" title="La L\xc3\xadnea de la Concepci\xc3\xb3n">La L\xc3\xadnea de la Concepci\xc3\xb3n</a>, a <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_in_C%C3%A1diz" title="List of municipalities in C\xc3\xa1diz">municipality</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_C%C3%A1diz" title="Province of C\xc3\xa1diz">province of C\xc3\xa1diz</a>, lies on the Spanish side of the border. The Spanish hinterland forms the <a href="/wiki/Comarca" title="Comarca">comarca</a> of <a href="/wiki/Campo_de_Gibraltar" title="Campo de Gibraltar">Campo de Gibraltar</a> (literally "Countryside of Gibraltar"). The shoreline measures 12 kilometres (7.5&#160;mi) in length. There are two coasts ("Sides") of Gibraltar: the East Side, which contains the settlements of <a href="/wiki/Sandy_Bay,_Gibraltar" title="Sandy Bay, Gibraltar">Sandy Bay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Catalan_Bay" title="Catalan Bay">Catalan Bay</a>; and the <a href="/wiki/Westside_(Gibraltar)" class="mw-redirect" title="Westside (Gibraltar)">Westside</a>, where the vast majority of the population lives. Gibraltar has no administrative divisions but is divided into seven <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Major_Residential_Areas" title="Gibraltar Major Residential Areas">Major Residential Areas</a>.\n</p><p>Having negligible <a href="/wiki/Natural_resource" title="Natural resource">natural resources</a> and few natural <a href="/wiki/Freshwater" class="mw-redirect" title="Freshwater">freshwater</a> resources, limited to natural wells in the north, until recently Gibraltar used large concrete and/or natural rock <a href="/wiki/Drainage_basin" title="Drainage basin">water catchments</a> to collect rainwater. Fresh water from the boreholes is supplemented by two <a href="/wiki/Desalination" title="Desalination">desalination</a> plants: a <a href="/wiki/Reverse_osmosis" title="Reverse osmosis">reverse osmosis</a> plant, constructed in a tunnel within the rock, and a <a href="/wiki/Multi-stage_flash_distillation" title="Multi-stage flash distillation">multi-stage flash distillation</a> plant at North Mole.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Gibraltar\'s terrain consists of the 426-metre-high (1,398&#160;ft) <a href="/wiki/Rock_of_Gibraltar" title="Rock of Gibraltar">Rock of Gibraltar</a><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> made of <a href="/wiki/Jurassic" title="Jurassic">Jurassic</a> <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a>, and the narrow coastal lowland surrounding it. It contains many tunnelled roads, most of which are still operated by the military and closed to the general public.\n</p>\n<div role="navigation" class="navbox" aria-labelledby="Places_adjacent_to_Gibraltar" style="padding:3px"><table class="nowraplinks collapsible autocollapse navbox-inner" style="border-spacing:0;background:transparent;color:inherit"><tbody><tr><th scope="col" class="navbox-title" colspan="2"><div id="Places_adjacent_to_Gibraltar" style="font-size:114%;margin:0 4em">Places adjacent to Gibraltar</div></th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="navbox-list navbox-odd" style="width:100%;padding:0px"><div style="padding:0em 0.25em"><table role="presentation" style="width:100%; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden; width:auto; max-width:1008px;">\n<div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:View_from_top_of_Gib_rock.jpg" class="image" title="Morocco (top far left across Strait); Spain: Algeciras (top centre across Bay of Gibraltar) and La Linea (right); Gibraltar cruise port and airport runway (right foreground); from the Rock"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/View_from_top_of_Gib_rock.jpg/1000px-View_from_top_of_Gib_rock.jpg" width="1000" height="165" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/View_from_top_of_Gib_rock.jpg/1500px-View_from_top_of_Gib_rock.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/View_from_top_of_Gib_rock.jpg/2000px-View_from_top_of_Gib_rock.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7966" data-file-height="1312" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:View_from_top_of_Gib_rock.jpg" title="File:View from top of Gib rock.jpg"> </a></div>Morocco (top far left across Strait); Spain: Algeciras (top centre across Bay of Gibraltar) and La Linea (right); Gibraltar cruise port and airport runway (right foreground); from the Rock</div>\n</div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Gibraltar" title="Climate of Gibraltar">Climate of Gibraltar</a></div>\n<p>Gibraltar has a <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification">K\xc3\xb6ppen climate classification</a> <i>Csa</i>),<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> with mild, rainy winters and warm, dry summers. As is the case for nearby <a href="/wiki/Algeciras" title="Algeciras">Algeciras</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tarifa" title="Tarifa">Tarifa</a>, summers are significantly cooler and annual temperature more constant than other cities on the southern coast of the Iberian peninsula because of its position on the Strait of Gibraltar. Rain occurs mainly in winter, with summer being generally dry. Its average annual temperature is about 22&#160;\xc2\xb0C (72&#160;\xc2\xb0F) as a daily high and 15&#160;\xc2\xb0C (59&#160;\xc2\xb0F) as the overnight low. In the coldest month, January, the high temperature averages 16.3&#160;\xc2\xb0C (61.3&#160;\xc2\xb0F) and the overnight low is 11&#160;\xc2\xb0C (52&#160;\xc2\xb0F) and the average sea temperature is 16&#160;\xc2\xb0C (61&#160;\xc2\xb0F). In the warmest month, August, the daily high temperature is 25&#160;\xc2\xb0C (77&#160;\xc2\xb0F), the overnight low is 20&#160;\xc2\xb0C (68&#160;\xc2\xb0F), and the average sea temperature is 22&#160;\xc2\xb0C (72&#160;\xc2\xb0F).<sup id="cite_ref-DWD_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DWD-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n<sup id="cite_ref-weather2travel_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-weather2travel-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable collapsible" style="width:90%; text-align:center; font-size:90%; line-height: 1.2em; margin:auto;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="14">Climate data for Gibraltar\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Month\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Jan\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Feb\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Mar\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Apr\n</th>\n<th scope="col">May\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Jun\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Jul\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Aug\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Sep\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Oct\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Nov\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Dec\n</th>\n<th scope="col" style="border-left-width:medium">Year\n</th></tr>\n<tr style="text-align: center;">\n<th scope="row" Met\xc3\xa9o Climat 1981-2010 (sun Deutscher Wetterdienst, 1961\xe2\x80\x931990)<sup id="cite_ref-DWD_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DWD-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n<p><sup id="cite_ref-DWDsun_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DWDsun-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;nb 1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flora_and_fauna">Flora and fauna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Flora and fauna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_mammals_of_Gibraltar" title="List of mammals of Gibraltar">List of mammals of Gibraltar</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_birds_of_Gibraltar" title="List of birds of Gibraltar">List of birds of Gibraltar</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_amphibians_and_reptiles_of_Gibraltar" title="List of amphibians and reptiles of Gibraltar">List of amphibians and reptiles of Gibraltar</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Iberis_gibraltarica.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Iberis_gibraltarica.JPG/220px-Iberis_gibraltarica.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Iberis_gibraltarica.JPG/330px-Iberis_gibraltarica.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Iberis_gibraltarica.JPG/440px-Iberis_gibraltarica.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1632" data-file-height="1088" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Iberis_gibraltarica.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Iberis_gibraltarica" title="Iberis gibraltarica">Gibraltar candytuft</a> growing at the <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Botanic_Gardens" title="Gibraltar Botanic Gardens">Gibraltar Botanic Gardens</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Common_dolphin_taken_by_Graham_Hesketh_of_Dolphin_Safari.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Common_dolphin_taken_by_Graham_Hesketh_of_Dolphin_Safari.png/220px-Common_dolphin_taken_by_Graham_Hesketh_of_Dolphin_Safari.png" width="220" height="121" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Common_dolphin_taken_by_Graham_Hesketh_of_Dolphin_Safari.png/330px-Common_dolphin_taken_by_Graham_Hesketh_of_Dolphin_Safari.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Common_dolphin_taken_by_Graham_Hesketh_of_Dolphin_Safari.png/440px-Common_dolphin_taken_by_Graham_Hesketh_of_Dolphin_Safari.png 2x" data-file-width="789" data-file-height="434" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Common_dolphin_taken_by_Graham_Hesketh_of_Dolphin_Safari.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Common_dolphin" title="Common dolphin">common dolphin</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Gibraltar" title="Bay of Gibraltar">Bay of Gibraltar</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Over 500 different species of <a href="/wiki/Flowering_plant" title="Flowering plant">flowering plants</a> grow on the Rock. Gibraltar is the only place in Europe where the <i>Gibraltar candytuft</i> (<i><a href="/wiki/Iberis_gibraltarica" title="Iberis gibraltarica">Iberis gibraltarica</a></i>) is found growing in the wild; the plant is otherwise native to North Africa. It is the symbol of the <a href="/wiki/Rock_of_Gibraltar#Upper_Rock_Nature_Reserve" title="Rock of Gibraltar">Upper Rock nature reserve</a>. <a href="/wiki/Olive" title="Olive">Olive</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pine" title="Pine">pine</a> trees are among the most common of those growing around the Rock.\n</p><p>Most of the Rock\'s upper area is covered by a <a href="/wiki/Nature_reserve" title="Nature reserve">nature reserve</a> which is home to around 230 <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Barbary_macaques" class="mw-redirect" title="Gibraltar Barbary macaques">Barbary macaques</a>, the famous "apes" of Gibraltar, which are actually <a href="/wiki/Monkey" title="Monkey">monkeys</a>. These are the only wild apes or monkeys found in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> This species, known scientifically as <i><a href="/wiki/Macaca_sylvanus" class="mw-redirect" title="Macaca sylvanus">Macaca sylvanus</a></i>, is listed as endangered by the <a href="/wiki/IUCN_Red_List" title="IUCN Red List">IUCN Red List</a> and is declining. Three-quarters of the world population live in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Atlas" title="Middle Atlas">Middle Atlas</a> mountains of <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>. Recent genetic studies and historical documents point to their presence on the Rock before its <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_Gibraltar" title="Capture of Gibraltar">capture by the British</a>, having possibly been introduced during the Islamic period. A superstition analogous to that of the <a href="/wiki/Raven" title="Raven">ravens</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Tower_of_London" title="Tower of London">Tower of London</a> states that if the apes ever leave, so will the British. In 1944, <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">British Prime Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a>, was so concerned about the dwindling population of apes that he sent a message to the <a href="/wiki/Chief_Secretary_(British_Empire)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chief Secretary (British Empire)">Colonial Secretary</a> requesting that something be done about the situation.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Other mammals found in Gibraltar include rabbits, foxes and bats. Dolphins and whales are frequently seen in the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Gibraltar" title="Bay of Gibraltar">Bay of Gibraltar</a>. Migrating birds are very common and Gibraltar is home to the only <a href="/wiki/Barbary_partridge" title="Barbary partridge">Barbary partridges</a> found on the European continent.\n</p><p>In 1991, Graham Watson, Gibraltar\'s <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Member of the European Parliament">MEP</a>, highlighted <a href="/wiki/Conservationism" class="mw-redirect" title="Conservationism">conservationists</a>\' fears that <a href="/wiki/Urban_development" class="mw-redirect" title="Urban development">urban development</a>, tourism and <a href="/wiki/Invasive_plant_species" class="mw-redirect" title="Invasive plant species">invasive plant species</a> were threatening Gibraltar\'s own plants as well as birds and <a href="/wiki/Bat_species" class="mw-redirect" title="Bat species">bat species</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">Environment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Environment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RockofGibraltar.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/RockofGibraltar.jpg/220px-RockofGibraltar.jpg" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/RockofGibraltar.jpg/330px-RockofGibraltar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/RockofGibraltar.jpg/440px-RockofGibraltar.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3903" data-file-height="2883" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RockofGibraltar.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Rock of Gibraltar (2010)</div></div></div>\n<p>In May 2016 a report by the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a> showed that Gibraltar had the worst air quality in any British territory. The report concentrated on <a href="/wiki/PM10" class="mw-redirect" title="PM10">PM10</a> and <a href="/wiki/PM2.5" class="mw-redirect" title="PM2.5">PM2.5</a> pollutants in the air.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Gibraltar" title="Economy of Gibraltar">Economy of Gibraltar</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Barbary_macaque_and_tourists.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Barbary_macaque_and_tourists.jpg/170px-Barbary_macaque_and_tourists.jpg" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Barbary_macaque_and_tourists.jpg/255px-Barbary_macaque_and_tourists.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Barbary_macaque_and_tourists.jpg/340px-Barbary_macaque_and_tourists.jpg 2x" data-file-width="666" data-file-height="998" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Barbary_macaque_and_tourists.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The semi-wild <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Barbary_macaques" class="mw-redirect" title="Gibraltar Barbary macaques">Barbary macaques</a> are an integral feature in <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Gibraltar" title="Tourism in Gibraltar">Gibraltar\'s tourism</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Defence_(United_Kingdom)" title="Ministry of Defence (United Kingdom)">British military</a> traditionally dominated <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Gibraltar" title="Economy of Gibraltar">Gibraltar\'s economy</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/Naval_dockyard" class="mw-redirect" title="Naval dockyard">naval dockyard</a> providing the bulk of economic activity. This, however, has diminished over the last 20 years, and is estimated to account for only 7 percent of the local economy, compared to over 60 percent in 1984. Today, Gibraltar\'s economy is dominated by four main sectors: <a href="/wiki/Offshore_financial_centre" title="Offshore financial centre">financial services</a>, <a href="/wiki/Online_gambling" title="Online gambling">online gambling</a>, shipping, and tourism, which includes duty-free retail sales to visitors.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> The territory also has a small manufacturing sector, with one company supplying ambulances produced from converted <a href="/wiki/SUV" class="mw-redirect" title="SUV">SUV</a> vehicles to the United Nations and other agencies.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the early 2000s, many <a href="/wiki/Bookmaker" title="Bookmaker">bookmakers</a> and online gaming operators moved to Gibraltar to benefit from operating in a regulated jurisdiction with a favourable <a href="/wiki/Corporate_tax" title="Corporate tax">corporate tax</a> regime. This corporate tax regime for non-resident controlled companies was phased out by January 2011 and replaced by a still favourable fixed corporate tax rate of 10 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Tourism is also a significant industry. Gibraltar is a popular port for cruise ships and attracts day visitors from resorts in Spain. The Rock is a popular tourist attraction, particularly among British tourists and residents in the southern coast of Spain. It is also a popular shopping destination, and all goods and services are <a href="/wiki/Value_added_tax" class="mw-redirect" title="Value added tax">VAT</a> free, but may be subject to Gibraltar taxes. Many of the large British high street chains have branches or franchises in Gibraltar including <a href="/wiki/Morrisons" title="Morrisons">Morrisons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marks_%26_Spencer" title="Marks &amp; Spencer">Marks &amp; Spencer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mothercare" title="Mothercare">Mothercare</a>. Branches and franchises of international retailers such as <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Hilfiger" title="Tommy Hilfiger">Tommy Hilfiger</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sunglass_Hut_International" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunglass Hut International">Sunglass Hut</a> are also present in Gibraltar, as is the Spanish clothing company <a href="/wiki/Mango_(clothing)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mango (clothing)">Mango</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Queensway_Quay_in_Gibraltar.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Queensway_Quay_in_Gibraltar.jpg/220px-Queensway_Quay_in_Gibraltar.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Queensway_Quay_in_Gibraltar.jpg/330px-Queensway_Quay_in_Gibraltar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Queensway_Quay_in_Gibraltar.jpg/440px-Queensway_Quay_in_Gibraltar.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Queensway_Quay_in_Gibraltar.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Queensway Quay Marina, along with <a href="/wiki/Ocean_Village,_Gibraltar" title="Ocean Village, Gibraltar">Ocean Village</a>, are two exclusive residential districts</div></div></div>\n<p>A number of <a href="/wiki/List_of_banks_in_Gibraltar" title="List of banks in Gibraltar">British and international banks</a> have operations based in Gibraltar. <a href="/wiki/Jyske_Bank" title="Jyske Bank">Jyske Bank</a> claims to be the oldest bank in the country, based on Jyske\'s acquisition in 1987 of <a href="/wiki/Banco_Galliano" title="Banco Galliano">Banco Galliano</a>, which began operations in Gibraltar in 1855. An ancestor of <a href="/wiki/Barclays" title="Barclays">Barclays</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Egyptian_Bank" title="Anglo-Egyptian Bank">Anglo-Egyptian Bank</a>, entered in 1888, and Credit Foncier (now <a href="/wiki/Cr%C3%A9dit_Agricole" title="Cr\xc3\xa9dit Agricole">Cr\xc3\xa9dit Agricole</a>) entered in 1920.\n</p><p>In 1967, Gibraltar enacted the Companies (Taxation and Concessions) Ordinance (now an Act), which provided for special tax treatment for international business.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> This was one of the factors leading to the growth of professional services such as <a href="/wiki/Private_banking" title="Private banking">private banking</a> and captive insurance management. Gibraltar has several attractive attributes as a <a href="/wiki/Financial_centre" title="Financial centre">financial centre</a>, including a <a href="/wiki/Common_law" title="Common law">common law</a> <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Gibraltar" title="Law of Gibraltar">legal system</a> and access to the EU single market in financial services. The Financial Services Commission (FSC),<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> which was established by an ordinance in 1989 (now an Act) that took effect in 1991, regulates the finance sector.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> In 1997, the Department of Trade and Industry established its Gibraltar Finance Centre (GFC) Division to facilitate the development the <a href="/wiki/Financial_sector_development" title="Financial sector development">financial sector development</a>. As of  2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, Gibraltar has 0.103 <a href="/wiki/Big_Four_(audit_firms)" class="mw-redirect" title="Big Four (audit firms)">Big Four</a> accounting firm offices per 1,000 population, the second highest in the world after the <a href="/wiki/British_Virgin_Islands" title="British Virgin Islands">British Virgin Islands</a>, and 0.6 banks per 1,000 people, the fifth most banks per capita in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> As of 2017, there is <a href="/wiki/Effect_of_Brexit_on_Gibraltar" title="Effect of Brexit on Gibraltar">very significant uncertainty</a> on continuing access to the EU single market after the forthcoming <a href="/wiki/Brexit" title="Brexit">Brexit</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-theguardian.com_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theguardian.com-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The currency of Gibraltar is the <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_pound" title="Gibraltar pound">Gibraltar pound</a>, issued by the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Gibraltar" title="Government of Gibraltar">Government of Gibraltar</a> under the terms of the 1934 <i>Currency Notes Act</i>. These banknotes are <a href="/wiki/Legal_tender" title="Legal tender">legal tender</a> in Gibraltar alongside Bank of England banknotes.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-currnotesact_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-currnotesact-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> In a <a href="/wiki/Currency_board" title="Currency board">currency board</a> arrangement, these notes are issued against reserves of <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">sterling</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-currnotesact_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-currnotesact-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> Clearing and settlement of funds is conducted in sterling.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Coins_of_the_Gibraltar_pound" class="mw-redirect" title="Coins of the Gibraltar pound">Coins</a> in circulation follow British denominations but have separate designs. Unofficially, most retail outlets in Gibraltar accept the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro</a>, though some payphones and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Gibraltar_Post_Office" title="Royal Gibraltar Post Office">Royal Gibraltar Post Office</a>, along with all other government offices, do not.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Gibraltar" title="Demographics of Gibraltar">Demographics of Gibraltar</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cathedral_of_St._Mary_the_Crowned_west.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Cathedral_of_St._Mary_the_Crowned_west.jpg/220px-Cathedral_of_St._Mary_the_Crowned_west.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Cathedral_of_St._Mary_the_Crowned_west.jpg/330px-Cathedral_of_St._Mary_the_Crowned_west.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Cathedral_of_St._Mary_the_Crowned_west.jpg/440px-Cathedral_of_St._Mary_the_Crowned_west.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="467" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cathedral_of_St._Mary_the_Crowned_west.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Roman Catholic <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_St._Mary_the_Crowned" title="Cathedral of St. Mary the Crowned">Cathedral of St. Mary the Crowned</a> was built in 1462 and is the territory\'s oldest Catholic church.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_Hindu_Temple_altar.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Gibraltar_Hindu_Temple_altar.JPG/220px-Gibraltar_Hindu_Temple_altar.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Gibraltar_Hindu_Temple_altar.JPG/330px-Gibraltar_Hindu_Temple_altar.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Gibraltar_Hindu_Temple_altar.JPG/440px-Gibraltar_Hindu_Temple_altar.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4352" data-file-height="2904" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_Hindu_Temple_altar.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Hindu_Temple" title="Gibraltar Hindu Temple">Gibraltar Hindu Temple</a>, opened in 2000</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mosque_of_Gibraltar.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Mosque_of_Gibraltar.jpg/220px-Mosque_of_Gibraltar.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Mosque_of_Gibraltar.jpg/330px-Mosque_of_Gibraltar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Mosque_of_Gibraltar.jpg/440px-Mosque_of_Gibraltar.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="1440" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mosque_of_Gibraltar.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Ibrahim-al-Ibrahim_Mosque" title="Ibrahim-al-Ibrahim Mosque">Ibrahim-al-Ibrahim Mosque</a> was a gift from <a href="/wiki/Fahd_of_Saudi_Arabia" title="Fahd of Saudi Arabia">King Fahd</a> of <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Gibraltar is one of the most densely populated territories in the world, with a usually-resident population in 2012 of 32,194 <sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> equivalent to approximately 4,959 inhabitants per square kilometre (12,840/sq&#160;mi). The growing demand for space is being increasingly met by <a href="/wiki/Land_reclamation" title="Land reclamation">land reclamation</a>; reclaimed land currently comprises approximately one tenth of the territory\'s total area.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Gibraltarian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Gibraltarian people">Gibraltarian people</a></div>\n<p>The demographics of Gibraltar reflect the many <a href="/wiki/European_ethnic_groups" class="mw-redirect" title="European ethnic groups">European</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Economic_migrant" title="Economic migrant">economic migrants</a> who came to the Rock over 300 years, after almost all of the Spanish population left in 1704.\n</p><p>Origin of surnames in the electoral roll by percentage is: British (27%), Spanish (26%, mostly <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">Andalusian</a> but also some 2% <a href="/wiki/Menorca" title="Menorca">Menorcan</a>), <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">Genoese</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Italians" title="Italians">Italian</a> (15%), <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a> (15%), and <a href="/wiki/Maltese_people" title="Maltese people">Maltese</a> (8%). There are also small (less than 1%) populations of other groups such as <a href="/wiki/Moroccan_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Moroccan people">Moroccans</a>, French, <a href="/wiki/Austrians" title="Austrians">Austrians</a>, Chinese, Japanese, <a href="/wiki/Polish_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Polish people">Polish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Danish_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Danish people">Danish</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable collapsible" style="font-size: 90%;">\n<caption><b> Usually-Resident Population and Persons Present in Gibraltar</b>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Resident Census\n</th>\n<th data-sort-type="number">1981<sup Gibraltarian, UK and other British and Moroccan.</small></dd></dl>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language">Language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Gibraltar" title="Languages of Gibraltar">Languages of Gibraltar</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a> of Gibraltar is English, and is used by the government and in schools. Most locals are <a href="/wiki/Multilingualism" title="Multilingualism">bilingual</a>, also speaking Spanish. However, because of the varied mix of ethnic groups which reside there, other languages are also spoken on the Rock. <a href="/wiki/Berber_languages" title="Berber languages">Berber</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a> are spoken by the <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Moroccan</a> community, as are <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sindhi_language" title="Sindhi language">Sindhi</a> by the Indian community. <a href="/wiki/Maltese_language" title="Maltese language">Maltese</a> is spoken by some families of <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Maltese_in_Gibraltar" title="History of the Maltese in Gibraltar">Maltese descent</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Archer2013_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Archer2013-82">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Gibraltarians often converse in <i><a href="/wiki/Llanito" title="Llanito">Llanito</a></i> (<small>pronounced&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[\xca\x8ea\xcb\x88nito]</a></span>),<sup id="cite_ref-creole_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-creole-83">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> a <a href="/wiki/Vernacular" title="Vernacular">vernacular</a> unique to Gibraltar. It is based on <a href="/wiki/Andalusian_Spanish" title="Andalusian Spanish">Andalusian Spanish</a> with a strong mixture of <a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">British English</a> and elements from languages such as Maltese, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Genoese_dialect" title="Genoese dialect">Genoese Italian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Haketia" title="Haketia">Haketia</a> (a <a href="/wiki/Judaeo-Spanish" title="Judaeo-Spanish">Judaeo-Spanish</a> dialect). Llanito also often involves <a href="/wiki/Code-switching" title="Code-switching">code-switching</a> to English and Spanish.\n</p><p>Gibraltarians often call themselves <i>Llanitos</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Kellermann2001_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kellermann2001-84">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="barbox tleft" style="overflow-x: auto;">\n<div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;">\n<table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">\n<tbody><tr style="background:#AAF"><th style="text-align:center;" colspan="5">Percentage of population by religion<sup id="cite_ref-gibraltar.gov.gi_5-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gibraltar.gov.gi-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></th></tr>\n<tr style="font-size:88%; text-align:right;"></td>\n<td style="padding:0 4px; text-align:right;">Percentage</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Roman Catholic</td>\n<td style="width: 100px;
