padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">7.1%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Other Christian</td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:#1C39BB; width:3.8%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">3.8%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Muslim</td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:#FF0000; width:3.6%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">3.6%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Jewish</td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:#0000FF; width:2.4%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">2.4%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Hindu</td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:#800080; width:2.0%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">2.0%</td>\n</tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;">Other/not stated</td>\n<td style="width: 100px; border-left: solid 1px silver; border-right: solid 1px silver;"><div style="background:#000000; width:1.3%; overflow: hidden;">&#8201;</div></td>\n<td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; text-align: right;">1.3%</td>\n</tr>\n\n</tbody></table>\n</div>\n</div><p>\nAccording to the 2012 census, approximately 72.1% of Gibraltarians are <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-85">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> The 16th century <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_Saint_Mary_the_Crowned" class="mw-redirect" title="Cathedral of Saint Mary the Crowned">Saint Mary the Crowned</a> is the cathedral church of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Gibraltar" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Gibraltar">Roman Catholic Diocese of Gibraltar</a>, and also the oldest Catholic church in the territory. Other Christian denominations include the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a> (7.7%), whose <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_the_Holy_Trinity,_Gibraltar" title="Cathedral of the Holy Trinity, Gibraltar">Cathedral of the Holy Trinity</a> is the cathedral of the Anglican <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Gibraltar_in_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Bishop of Gibraltar in Europe">Bishop of Gibraltar in Europe</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Methodist_Church" title="Gibraltar Methodist Church">Gibraltar Methodist Church</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Scotland" title="Church of Scotland">Church of Scotland</a>, various <a href="/wiki/Pentecostal" class="mw-redirect" title="Pentecostal">Pentecostal</a> and independent churches mostly influenced by the <a href="/wiki/House_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="House Church">House Church</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charismatic_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Charismatic movement">Charismatic movements</a>, as well as a <a href="/wiki/Plymouth_Brethren" title="Plymouth Brethren">Plymouth Brethren</a> congregation. Several of these congregations are represented by the Gibraltar Evangelical Alliance. </p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cathedral_of_the_Holy_Trinity.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Cathedral_of_the_Holy_Trinity.jpg/220px-Cathedral_of_the_Holy_Trinity.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Cathedral_of_the_Holy_Trinity.jpg/330px-Cathedral_of_the_Holy_Trinity.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Cathedral_of_the_Holy_Trinity.jpg/440px-Cathedral_of_the_Holy_Trinity.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="467" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cathedral_of_the_Holy_Trinity.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_the_Holy_Trinity,_Gibraltar" title="Cathedral of the Holy Trinity, Gibraltar">Cathedral of the Holy Trinity</a></div></div></div><p> There is also a <a href="/wiki/Ward_(LDS_Church)" title="Ward (LDS Church)">ward</a> of <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints</a>, and two congregations of <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses">Jehovah\'s Witnesses</a>. 7.1% advised that they have no religion. The Gibraltar Secular Humanist Society also holds regular meetings.\n</p><p>The third religion in size is <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> (3.6% of the population). There is also an established <a href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">Hindu</a> population (2%), members of the <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith" title="Bah\xc3\xa1&#39;\xc3\xad Faith">Bah\xc3\xa1\'\xc3\xad Faith</a> and a long-established <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Gibraltar" title="History of the Jews in Gibraltar">Jewish community</a>, which, at 763 persons, accounts for 2.4% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-85">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> As a share of the total population, this is the second-largest Jewish population in the world, trailing only <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>. There are four functioning <a href="/wiki/Synagogues_of_Gibraltar" title="Synagogues of Gibraltar">Orthodox synagogues in Gibraltar</a> and several kosher establishments.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Gibraltar" title="Education in Gibraltar">Education in Gibraltar</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Arms_of_The_University_of_Gibraltar.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/5e/The_Arms_of_The_University_of_Gibraltar.JPG" width="170" height="182" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="170" data-file-height="182" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Arms_of_The_University_of_Gibraltar.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Arms of The University of Gibraltar</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Education_in_Gibraltar" title="Education in Gibraltar">Education in Gibraltar</a> generally follows the <a href="/wiki/Education_in_England" title="Education in England">English model</a>, operating within a <a href="/wiki/Three-tier_education" title="Three-tier education">three tier system</a>. Schools in Gibraltar use the <a href="/wiki/Key_Stage" title="Key Stage">Key Stage</a> modular approach to teach the <a href="/wiki/National_Curriculum_(England,_Wales_and_Northern_Ireland)" title="National Curriculum (England, Wales and Northern Ireland)">National Curriculum</a>. Gibraltar has 15 <a href="/wiki/State_school" title="State school">state schools</a>, two private schools and a college of further education, <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_College" title="Gibraltar College">Gibraltar College</a>. Government secondary schools are <a href="/wiki/Bayside_Comprehensive_School_(Gibraltar)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bayside Comprehensive School (Gibraltar)">Bayside Comprehensive School</a> for boys and <a href="/wiki/Westside_School_(Gibraltar)" class="mw-redirect" title="Westside School (Gibraltar)">Westside School</a> for girls, and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Prior_Park_School_Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Prior Park School Gibraltar (page does not exist)">Prior Park School Gibraltar</a> is an independent coeducational secondary school.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 31 March 2015 the government of Gibraltar announced the adoption of the University of Gibraltar Act and The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Gibraltar" title="University of Gibraltar">University of Gibraltar</a> opened in September 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> Previously, there were no facilities in Gibraltar for full-time higher education, and consequently, all Gibraltarian students studied elsewhere at <a href="/wiki/Academic_degree" title="Academic degree">degree</a> level or its equivalent and also for certain non-degree courses.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> The Government of Gibraltar operates a scholarship/grant system to provide funding for students studying in the United Kingdom. All Gibraltarian students used to follow the <a href="/wiki/Student_loans_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Student loans in the United Kingdom">UK student loans procedure</a>, applying for a loan from the <a href="/wiki/Student_Loans_Company" title="Student Loans Company">Student Loans Company</a> which was then reimbursed in full by the Government of Gibraltar. In August 2010, this system was replaced by the direct payment by the government of grants and tuition fees. The overwhelming majority of Gibraltarians continue their studies at university level.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health_care">Health care</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Health care">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>All Gibraltarians are entitled to health care in public <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/ward" class="extiw" title="wikt:ward">wards</a> and clinics at <a href="/wiki/St_Bernard%27s_Hospital" title="St Bernard&#39;s Hospital">St Bernard\'s Hospital</a> and <a href="/wiki/Primary_health_care" class="mw-redirect" title="Primary health care">primary health care</a> centre. All other British citizens are also entitled to free-of-charge treatment on the Rock on presentation of a valid <a href="/wiki/British_passport" title="British passport">British passport</a> during stays of up to 30 days. Other EU nationals are equally entitled to treatment on presentation of a valid <a href="/wiki/European_Health_Insurance_Card" title="European Health Insurance Card">European Health Insurance Card</a>. <a href="/wiki/Dental_surgery" title="Dental surgery">Dental treatment</a> and <a href="/wiki/Prescription_drug" title="Prescription drug">prescribed medicines</a> are free of charge for Gibraltarian students and <a href="/wiki/Pensioner" title="Pensioner">pensioners</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Health_Authority" title="Gibraltar Health Authority">Gibraltar Health Authority</a> is funded through the <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Group_Practice_Medical_Scheme" title="Gibraltar Group Practice Medical Scheme">Gibraltar Group Practice Medical Scheme</a>. It employs around 900 people, handling 37,000 <a href="/wiki/Accident_and_emergency" class="mw-redirect" title="Accident and emergency">A&amp;E</a> attendances, 40,000 outpatient appointments, and 90,000 <a href="/wiki/General_practitioner" title="General practitioner">GP</a> visits a year. Some specialist care is provided by visiting consultants and in UK and Spanish hospitals. First-line medical and nursing services are provided at the Primary Care Centre, which has 16 GPs, with more specialised services available at <a href="/wiki/St_Bernard%27s_Hospital" title="St Bernard&#39;s Hospital">St Bernard\'s Hospital</a>, a 210-bed civilian hospital opened in 2005. Psychiatric care is provided by <a href="/wiki/King_George_V_Hospital_(Gibraltar)" title="King George V Hospital (Gibraltar)">King George V Hospital</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Gibraltar" title="Culture of Gibraltar">Culture of Gibraltar</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_Tercentenary_flag_display.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Gibraltar_Tercentenary_flag_display.jpg/220px-Gibraltar_Tercentenary_flag_display.jpg" width="220" height="341" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c4/Gibraltar_Tercentenary_flag_display.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="465" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_Tercentenary_flag_display.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Tercentenary" class="mw-redirect" title="Tercentenary">Tercentenary</a> celebrations in Gibraltar.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Gibraltar" title="Culture of Gibraltar">culture of Gibraltar</a> reflects Gibraltarians\' diverse origins. While there are Spanish (mostly from nearby <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">Andalusia</a>) and British influences, the ethnic origins of most Gibraltarians are not confined to these ethnicities. Other ethnicities include <a href="/wiki/Genoa" title="Genoa">Genoese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maltese_people" title="Maltese people">Maltese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">German</a>. A few other Gibraltar residents are <a href="/wiki/Sephardi_Jews" title="Sephardi Jews">Jewish of Sephardic</a> origin, <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Moroccan</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Non-resident_Indian_and_person_of_Indian_origin" title="Non-resident Indian and person of Indian origin">Indians</a>. British influence remains strong, with English being the language of government, commerce, education and the media.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_sovereignty_referendum,_1967" title="Gibraltar sovereignty referendum, 1967">Gibraltar\'s first sovereignty referendum</a> is celebrated annually on <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_National_Day" title="Gibraltar National Day">Gibraltar National Day</a> (10 September). It is a public holiday, during which most Gibraltarians dress in their <a href="/wiki/National_colours" title="National colours">national colours</a> of red and white. Until 2016, the tradition had been to also release 30,000 similarly coloured balloons, which represented the people of Gibraltar. However, this tradition has now been ended because of the threat that it poses to wildlife, particularly marine.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> The 300th anniversary of <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_Gibraltar" title="Capture of Gibraltar">Gibraltar\'s capture</a> was celebrated in 2004 on Tercentenary Day (4 August), when in recognition of and with thanks for its long association with Gibraltar, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> was given the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Freedom_of_the_City_of_Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Freedom of the City of Gibraltar (page does not exist)">Freedom of the City of Gibraltar</a> and a human chain of Gibraltarians dressed in red, white and blue, linked hands to encircle the Rock. On 4 June 2012, the <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Diamond_Jubilee_Flotilla" title="Gibraltar Diamond Jubilee Flotilla">Gibraltar Diamond Jubilee Flotilla</a>, inspired by the <a href="/wiki/Thames_Diamond_Jubilee_Pageant" title="Thames Diamond Jubilee Pageant">Thames Diamond Jubilee Pageant</a>, celebrated sixty years of the <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen Elizabeth II">Queen</a>\'s reign.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Broadcasting_Corporation" title="Gibraltar Broadcasting Corporation">Gibraltar Broadcasting Corporation</a> operates a television and radio station on UHF, VHF and medium-wave. The radio service is also internet-streamed. Special events and the daily news bulletin are streamed in video. The other local radio service is operated by the <a href="/wiki/British_Forces_Broadcasting_Service" title="British Forces Broadcasting Service">British Forces Broadcasting Service</a> which also provides a limited cable television network to HM Forces. The largest and most frequently published newspaper is the <i><a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Chronicle" title="Gibraltar Chronicle">Gibraltar Chronicle</a></i>, Gibraltar\'s oldest established daily newspaper and the world\'s second oldest English language newspaper to have been in print continuously<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> with daily editions six days a week. <i><a href="/wiki/Panorama_(Gibraltar)" title="Panorama (Gibraltar)">Panorama</a></i> is published on weekdays, and <i>7 Days</i>, <i>The New People</i>, and <i>Gibsport</i> are weekly.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_National_Day_027_(9719742224)_(2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Gibraltar_National_Day_027_%289719742224%29_%282%29.jpg/220px-Gibraltar_National_Day_027_%289719742224%29_%282%29.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Gibraltar_National_Day_027_%289719742224%29_%282%29.jpg/330px-Gibraltar_National_Day_027_%289719742224%29_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Gibraltar_National_Day_027_%289719742224%29_%282%29.jpg/440px-Gibraltar_National_Day_027_%289719742224%29_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1969" data-file-height="1310" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_National_Day_027_(9719742224)_(2).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Thousands of <a href="/wiki/Gibraltarian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Gibraltarian people">Gibraltarians</a> dress in their national colours of red and white during the 2013 <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_National_Day" title="Gibraltar National Day">Gibraltar National Day</a> celebrations.</div></div></div>\n<p>Native Gibraltarians have produced some literature of note. The first in fiction was probably <a href="/wiki/H%C3%A9ctor_Licudi" title="H\xc3\xa9ctor Licudi">H\xc3\xa9ctor Licudi</a>\'s 1929 novel <i>Barbarita</i>, written in Spanish,<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> chronicling the largely autobiographical adventures of a young Gibraltarian man. Throughout the 1940s and 1950s, several anthologies of poetry were published by <a href="/wiki/Leopoldo_Sanguinetti" title="Leopoldo Sanguinetti">Leopoldo Sanguinetti</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Albert_Joseph_Patron&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Albert Joseph Patron (page does not exist)">Albert Joseph Patron</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alberto_Pizzarello" title="Alberto Pizzarello">Alberto Pizzarello</a>. The 1960s were largely dominated by the theatrical works of <a href="/wiki/Elio_Cruz" title="Elio Cruz">Elio Cruz</a> and his two highly acclaimed Spanish language plays <i>La Lola se va p\xc3\xa1 Londre</i> and <i>Connie con cama camera en el comedor</i>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> In the 1990s, the Gibraltarian <a href="/wiki/Intellectual" title="Intellectual">man-of-letters</a> <a href="/wiki/Mario_Arroyo" title="Mario Arroyo">Mario Arroyo</a> published <i>Profiles</i> (1994), a series of bilingual meditations on love, loneliness and death. <a href="/wiki/Trino_Cruz" title="Trino Cruz">Trino Cruz</a> is a bilingual poet originally writing English but now mainly in Spanish, who also translates <a href="/wiki/Maghreb" title="Maghreb">Maghreb</a> poetry.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ElPais_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ElPais-97">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-T\xc3\xa9llez2013_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-T\xc3\xa9llez2013-98">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> Of late there have been works by the essayist <a href="/wiki/Mary_Chiappe" title="Mary Chiappe">Mary Chiappe</a>, such as her volume of essays <i>Cabbages and Kings</i> (2006) and by <a href="/wiki/M._G._Sanchez" title="M. G. Sanchez">M. G. Sanchez</a>, author of the books <i>Rock Black: Ten Gibraltarian Stories</i> (2008) and <i>Diary of a Victorian Colonial</i> (2009). Mary Chiappe and <a href="/wiki/Sam_Benady" title="Sam Benady">Sam Benady</a> have also published a series of detective books centred on the character of the nineteenth-century Gibraltarian sleuth Bresciano.\n</p><p>Musicians from Gibraltar include <a href="/wiki/Charles_Ramirez" title="Charles Ramirez">Charles Ramirez</a>, the first guitarist invited to play with the <a href="/wiki/Royal_College_of_Music" title="Royal College of Music">Royal College of Music</a> Orchestra,<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> successful rock bands like <a href="/wiki/Breed_77" title="Breed 77">Breed 77</a>, <a href="/wiki/Melon_Diesel" title="Melon Diesel">Melon Diesel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Taxi_(Gibraltar_band)" title="Taxi (Gibraltar band)">Taxi</a>, while Gibraltarian bassist Glen Diani played for Irish/British <a href="/wiki/Nu_metal" title="Nu metal">nu metal</a> group <a href="/wiki/One_Minute_Silence" title="One Minute Silence">One Minute Silence</a>. <a href="/wiki/Albert_Hammond" title="Albert Hammond">Albert Hammond</a> had top 10 hits in the UK and US and has written many songs for international artists such as <a href="/wiki/Whitney_Houston" title="Whitney Houston">Whitney Houston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tina_Turner" title="Tina Turner">Tina Turner</a> and <a href="/wiki/Julio_Iglesias" title="Julio Iglesias">Julio Iglesias</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Gibraltarian cuisine is the result of a long relationship between the Andalusian Spaniards and the British, as well as the many foreigners who made Gibraltar their home over the past three centuries. The culinary influences include those from Malta, Genoa, Portugal, Andalusia and Britain. This marriage of tastes has given Gibraltar an eclectic mix of Mediterranean and British cuisine. <a href="/wiki/Profiteroles" class="mw-redirect" title="Profiteroles">Profiteroles</a>, a French <a href="/wiki/Choux_pastry" title="Choux pastry">choux pastry</a> ball with a sweet <a href="/wiki/Filling_(cooking)" class="mw-redirect" title="Filling (cooking)">filling</a> of whipped cream, is considered to be Gibraltar\'s <a href="/wiki/National_dish" title="National dish">national dish</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> These are often served after a meal including <a href="/wiki/Calentita" class="mw-redirect" title="Calentita">Calentita</a>, a baked bread-like dish made with <a href="/wiki/Gram_flour" title="Gram flour">chickpea flour</a>, water, olive oil, salt and pepper.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Gibraltar" title="Sport in Gibraltar">Sport in Gibraltar</a></div>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <small><i>(July 2011)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_starting_XI.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Gibraltar_starting_XI.jpg/220px-Gibraltar_starting_XI.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Gibraltar_starting_XI.jpg/330px-Gibraltar_starting_XI.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Gibraltar_starting_XI.jpg/440px-Gibraltar_starting_XI.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1969" data-file-height="1310" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_starting_XI.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_national_football_team" title="Gibraltar national football team">Gibraltar national football team</a> lining up in their first official match in 2013</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2007, there were 18 Gibraltar sports associations with official recognition from their respective international <a href="/wiki/Sport_governing_body" class="mw-redirect" title="Sport governing body">governing bodies</a>. Others have submitted applications for recognition which are being considered. The government supports the many sporting associations financially. Gibraltar also competes in the bi-annual <a href="/wiki/International_Island_Games_Association" title="International Island Games Association">Island Games</a>, which it hosted in 1995.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Football_in_Gibraltar" title="Football in Gibraltar">Football</a> is a popular sport in Gibraltar. The <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Football_Association" title="Gibraltar Football Association">Gibraltar Football Association</a> applied for full membership of <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a>, but their bid was turned down in 2007 in a contentious decision.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_Sport_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Sport-102">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>\nGibraltar was confirmed as UEFA\'s 54th member on 24 May 2013 as a result of <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Arbitration_for_Sport" title="Court of Arbitration for Sport">Court of Arbitration for Sport</a> (CAS) arbitration and played in <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016" title="UEFA Euro 2016">Euro 2016</a> qualifications.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-104">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Their first match was a 0\xe2\x80\x930 draw against Slovakia. Gibraltar\'s national team won its first-ever match in UEFA competition on 13 October 2018, beating Armenia in the <a href="/wiki/2018%E2%80%9319_UEFA_Nations_League_D" title="2018\xe2\x80\x9319 UEFA Nations League D">2018\xe2\x80\x9319 UEFA Nations League D</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Subsequently, Gibraltar applied for FIFA membership but this bid was also turned down. On 2 May 2016 the CAS upheld the appeal filed by the Gibraltar Football Association regarding its request to become a full-time member of FIFA. CAS ordered FIFA to stop blocking Gibraltar\'s application for membership and allow it "without delay".<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Cricket_Association" title="Gibraltar Cricket Association">Cricket</a> enjoys popularity in Gibraltar. The <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_national_cricket_team" title="Gibraltar national cricket team">Gibraltar national cricket team</a> won the <a href="/wiki/European_Cricket_Championship" title="European Cricket Championship">European Cricket Championship</a> Division Two in 2000 and 2002. \n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Rugby_union_in_Gibraltar" title="Rugby union in Gibraltar">Rugby union</a> is fairly popular and one of the fastest growing team sports. <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Rugby_Football_Union" title="Gibraltar Rugby Football Union">Gibraltar Rugby Football Union</a> applied for membership of Europe\'s governing body for rugby. Gibraltar is believed to be the birthplace of the rugby variant <a href="/wiki/Tag_Rugby" class="mw-redirect" title="Tag Rugby">Tag Rugby</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;nb 2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar_Rifle_Association&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Gibraltar Rifle Association (page does not exist)">Gibraltar Rifle Association</a> (GRA) was Gibraltar\'s most successful team at the 2009 Island Games, earning four gold medals.\n</p><p>Darts is also a popular sport, with the Gibraltar Darts Association (a full member of World Darts Federation since 1977) running leagues and other regular tournaments. In 2010, Gibraltar hosted and won the Mediterranean Cup, competing against France, Italy, Turkey, Malta and Cyprus.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Communications">Communications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Communications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Telex1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Telex1.jpg/220px-Telex1.jpg" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Telex1.jpg/330px-Telex1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7c/Telex1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="260" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Telex1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A plaque in City Mill Lane marking the site of Gibraltar\'s first telephone exchange.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Victorian_Post_Box_of_1887_in_use_at_Gibraltar_in_2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Victorian_Post_Box_of_1887_in_use_at_Gibraltar_in_2008.jpg/170px-Victorian_Post_Box_of_1887_in_use_at_Gibraltar_in_2008.jpg" width="170" height="282" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Victorian_Post_Box_of_1887_in_use_at_Gibraltar_in_2008.jpg/255px-Victorian_Post_Box_of_1887_in_use_at_Gibraltar_in_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Victorian_Post_Box_of_1887_in_use_at_Gibraltar_in_2008.jpg/340px-Victorian_Post_Box_of_1887_in_use_at_Gibraltar_in_2008.jpg 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="848" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Victorian_Post_Box_of_1887_in_use_at_Gibraltar_in_2008.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Victorian post box of standard 1887 UK design in use in Gibraltar\'s Main Street (2008).</div></div></div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Communications_in_Gibraltar" title="Communications in Gibraltar">Communications in Gibraltar</a></div>\n<p>Gibraltar has a digital <a href="/wiki/Telephone_exchange" title="Telephone exchange">telephone exchange</a> supported by a <a href="/wiki/Optical_fibre" class="mw-redirect" title="Optical fibre">fibre optic</a> and copper infrastructure; the telephone operator <a href="/wiki/Gibtelecom" title="Gibtelecom">Gibtelecom</a> also operates a <a href="/wiki/GSM" title="GSM">GSM</a> network. Internet connectivity is available across the fixed network. Gibraltar\'s top-level domain code is <a href="/wiki/.gi" title=".gi">.gi</a>.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/International_Direct_Dialling" class="mw-redirect" title="International Direct Dialling">International Direct Dialling</a> (IDD) is provided, and Gibraltar was allocated the access code <a href="/wiki/%2B350" class="mw-redirect" title="+350">+350</a> by the <a href="/wiki/International_Telecommunication_Union" title="International Telecommunication Union">International Telecommunication Union</a>. This has been universally valid since 10 February 2007, when the <a href="/wiki/Telecom_dispute_between_Gibraltar_and_Spain" title="Telecom dispute between Gibraltar and Spain">telecom dispute</a> was resolved.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Gibraltar" title="Transport in Gibraltar">Transport in Gibraltar</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_Cable_Car_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Gibraltar_Cable_Car_2.jpg/170px-Gibraltar_Cable_Car_2.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Gibraltar_Cable_Car_2.jpg/255px-Gibraltar_Cable_Car_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Gibraltar_Cable_Car_2.jpg/340px-Gibraltar_Cable_Car_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2136" data-file-height="2848" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_Cable_Car_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Cable_Car" title="Gibraltar Cable Car">Gibraltar Cable Car</a> runs from outside the <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Botanic_Gardens" title="Gibraltar Botanic Gardens">Gibraltar Botanic Gardens</a> to the top of the Rock.</div></div></div>\n<p>Within Gibraltar, the main form of transport is the car. <a href="/wiki/Motorcycle" title="Motorcycle">Motorcycles</a> are also very popular and there is a good modern bus service. Unlike in the UK and other British territories, traffic <a href="/wiki/Right-_and_left-hand_traffic" class="mw-redirect" title="Right- and left-hand traffic">drives on the right</a> and speed limits are in km/h, as the territory shares a land border with Spain. The <a href="/wiki/European_route_E15" title="European route E15">E15</a> highway connecting Spain, France, and the United Kingdom is accessible from the Spanish side using the <a href="/wiki/Autov%C3%ADa_CA-34" title="Autov\xc3\xada CA-34">CA-34</a> <a href="/wiki/Autov%C3%ADa" title="Autov\xc3\xada">autov\xc3\xada</a>.\n</p><p>There is a <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Cable_Car" title="Gibraltar Cable Car">Gibraltar Cable Car</a> that runs from ground level to the top of the Rock, with an intermediate station at <a href="/w/index.php?title=Apes%27_Den&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Apes&#39; Den (page does not exist)">Apes\' Den</a>.\n</p><p>Restrictions on transport introduced by Spanish dictator <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">Francisco Franco</a> closed the land frontier in 1969 and also prohibited any air or ferry connections. In 1982, the land border was reopened. As the result of an agreement signed in <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B3rdoba,_Spain" title="C\xc3\xb3rdoba, Spain">C\xc3\xb3rdoba</a> on 18 September 2006 between Gibraltar, the United Kingdom and Spain,<sup id="cite_ref-cordoba_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cordoba-109">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> the Spanish government agreed to relax <a href="/wiki/Border_control" title="Border control">border controls</a> at the frontier that have plagued locals for decades; in return, Britain paid increased pensions to Spanish workers who lost their jobs when Franco closed the border.<sup id="cite_ref-pensions_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pensions-110">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> Telecommunication restrictions were lifted in February 2007 and air links with Spain were restored in December 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-airport_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-airport-111">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The border control is the only road border control between two EU members that is expected to remain indefinitely (Bulgaria, Croatia and Romania have border controls which are expected to <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area#Prospective_members" title="Schengen Area">be removed around 2020</a>), however Britain plans to leave the EU. Motorists and pedestrians crossing the border with Spain are occasionally subjected to very long delays.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Spain has occasionally closed the border during disputes or incidents involving the Gibraltar authorities, such as the <a href="/wiki/MV_Aurora_(2000)#Norovirus_breakout" title="MV Aurora (2000)"><i>Aurora</i> cruise ship incident</a><sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> and when fishermen from the Spanish fishing vessel <i>Pira\xc3\xb1a</i> were arrested for illegal fishing in Gibraltar waters.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Air">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_International_Airport" title="Gibraltar International Airport">Gibraltar International Airport</a></div>\n<p>As of 2017, Gibraltar maintains regular flight connections with London, <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bristol" title="Bristol">Bristol</a> in the UK, and with <a href="/wiki/Casablanca" title="Casablanca">Casablanca</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tangier" title="Tangier">Tangier</a> in <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/GB_Airways" title="GB Airways">GB Airways</a> operated a service between Gibraltar and London and other cities for many years. The airline initially flew under the name "Gibraltar Airways". In 1989, and in anticipation of service to cities outside the UK, Gibraltar Airways changed its name to GB Airways with the belief that a new name would incur fewer political problems. As a franchise, the airline operated flights in full <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a> livery. In 2007,&#160;GB Airways was purchased by <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">easyJet</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> which began operating flights under their name in April 2008 when British Airways re-introduced flights to Gibraltar under their name. EasyJet have since added <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Airport" title="Bristol Airport">Bristol</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport" title="Manchester Airport">Manchester</a> and also operated flights to <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Liverpool Airport">Liverpool</a> between 2011 and 2012. Until entering administration in October 2017, <a href="/wiki/Monarch_Airlines" title="Monarch Airlines">Monarch Airlines</a> operated the largest number of flights between the United Kingdom and Gibraltar, with scheduled services between Gibraltar and <a href="/wiki/London_Luton_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="London Luton Airport">Luton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport" title="Gatwick Airport">London Gatwick</a>, <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_Airport" title="Birmingham Airport">Birmingham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport" title="Manchester Airport">Manchester</a>. The Spanish <a href="/wiki/National_airline" class="mw-redirect" title="National airline">national airline</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iberia_Airlines" class="mw-redirect" title="Iberia Airlines">Iberia</a>, operated a daily service to <a href="/wiki/Barajas_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Barajas Airport">Madrid</a> which ceased for lack of demand. In May 2009, <a href="/wiki/%C3%81ndalus_L%C3%ADneas_A%C3%A9reas" title="\xc3\x81ndalus L\xc3\xadneas A\xc3\xa9reas">\xc3\x81ndalus L\xc3\xadneas A\xc3\xa9reas</a> opened a Spanish service,<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> which also ceased operations in March 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> An annual return <a href="/wiki/Charter_flight" class="mw-redirect" title="Charter flight">charter flight</a> to <a href="/wiki/Malta_International_Airport" title="Malta International Airport">Malta</a> is operated by <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Maltese</a> national airline, <a href="/wiki/Air_Malta" title="Air Malta">Air Malta</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_Airport_Main_Highway.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Gibraltar_Airport_Main_Highway.jpg/220px-Gibraltar_Airport_Main_Highway.jpg" width="220" height="125" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Gibraltar_Airport_Main_Highway.jpg/330px-Gibraltar_Airport_Main_Highway.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Gibraltar_Airport_Main_Highway.jpg/440px-Gibraltar_Airport_Main_Highway.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2211" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_Airport_Main_Highway.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The main road that crosses Gibraltar Airport.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_Airport_New_Terminal.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Gibraltar_Airport_New_Terminal.jpg/220px-Gibraltar_Airport_New_Terminal.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Gibraltar_Airport_New_Terminal.jpg/330px-Gibraltar_Airport_New_Terminal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Gibraltar_Airport_New_Terminal.jpg/440px-Gibraltar_Airport_New_Terminal.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar_Airport_New_Terminal.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The new terminal at Gibraltar Airport.</div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Gibraltar Airport">Gibraltar International Airport</a> is unusual not only because of its proximity to the city centre resulting in the airport terminal being within walking distance of much of Gibraltar but also because the runway intersects <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill_Avenue" title="Winston Churchill Avenue">Winston Churchill Avenue</a>, the main north-south street, requiring movable barricades to close when aircraft land or depart. New roads and a tunnel, which will end the need to stop road traffic when aircraft use the runway, were planned to coincide with the building of a new <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Airport#New_terminal" class="mw-redirect" title="Gibraltar Airport">airport terminal building</a> with an originally estimated completion date of 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-pressnote_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pressnote-120">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> although it has not been completed because of delays.\n</p><p>The most popular alternative airport for Gibraltar is <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1laga_Airport" title="M\xc3\xa1laga Airport">M\xc3\xa1laga Airport</a> in Spain, some 120 kilometres (75&#160;mi) to the east, which offers a wide range of destinations, second to <a href="/wiki/Jerez_Airport" title="Jerez Airport">Jerez Airport</a> which is closer to Gibraltar. In addition, the <a href="/wiki/Algeciras_Heliport" title="Algeciras Heliport">Algeciras Heliport</a> across the bay offers scheduled services to <a href="/wiki/Ceuta" title="Ceuta">Ceuta</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sea">Sea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Sea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Cruise_Terminal" title="Gibraltar Cruise Terminal">Gibraltar Cruise Terminal</a> receives a large number of visits from <a href="/wiki/Cruise_ship" title="Cruise ship">cruise ships</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">Strait of Gibraltar</a> is one of the busiest shipping lanes in the world.\n</p><p>Passenger and cargo ships anchor in the <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Harbour" class="mw-redirect" title="Gibraltar Harbour">Gibraltar Harbour</a>. Also, a ferry links Gibraltar with <a href="/wiki/Tangier" title="Tangier">Tangier</a> in Morocco. The ferry between Gibraltar and <a href="/wiki/Algeciras" title="Algeciras">Algeciras</a>, which had been halted in 1969 when Franco severed communications with Gibraltar, was finally reopened on 16 December 2009, served by the Spanish company <a href="/w/index.php?title=Transcoma&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Transcoma (page does not exist)">Transcoma</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Ferries by FRS running twice a week from Gibraltar to <a href="/wiki/Tanger-Med" title="Tanger-Med">Tanger-Med</a> port provide access to the <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Morocco" title="Rail transport in Morocco">Moroccan railway</a> system.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>While railway track extends to the outskirts of <a href="/wiki/La_L%C3%ADnea_de_la_Concepci%C3%B3n" title="La L\xc3\xadnea de la Concepci\xc3\xb3n">La L\xc3\xadnea</a> from an <a href="/wiki/San_Roque-La_L%C3%ADnea_railway" class="mw-redirect" title="San Roque-La L\xc3\xadnea railway">aborted rail expansion project in the 1970s</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> the closest railway station in Spain is <a href="/wiki/San_Roque_station" title="San Roque station">San Roque station</a>, accessible via buses from <a href="/wiki/La_L%C3%ADnea_de_la_Concepci%C3%B3n" title="La L\xc3\xadnea de la Concepci\xc3\xb3n">La L\xc3\xadnea</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Water_supply_and_sanitation">Water supply and sanitation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Water supply and sanitation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_Gibraltar" title="Water supply and sanitation in Gibraltar">Water supply and sanitation in Gibraltar</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Water_supply" title="Water supply">Water supply</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sanitation" title="Sanitation">sanitation</a> in Gibraltar have been major concerns for its inhabitants throughout its history. There are no rivers, streams, or large bodies of water on the peninsula. Gibraltar\'s water supply was formerly provided by a combination of an aqueduct, wells, and the use of cisterns, barrels and earthenware pots to capture rainwater. This became increasingly inadequate as Gibraltar\'s population grew in the 18th and 19th centuries and lethal diseases such as <a href="/wiki/Cholera" title="Cholera">cholera</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yellow_fever" title="Yellow fever">yellow fever</a> began to spread. In the late 19th century, a Sanitary Commission instigated major improvements which saw the introduction of large-scale desalination and the use of giant water catchments covering over 2.5 million square feet (nearly 250,000 m<sup>2</sup>). Today Gibraltar\'s supply of drinking water comes entirely from <a href="/wiki/Desalination" title="Desalination">desalination</a>, with a separate supply of saltwater for sanitary purposes. Both supplies are delivered from huge underground reservoirs excavated under the <a href="/wiki/Rock_of_Gibraltar" title="Rock of Gibraltar">Rock of Gibraltar</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Police">Police</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Police">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Royal_Gibraltar_Police" title="Royal Gibraltar Police">Royal Gibraltar Police</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Defence_Police" title="Gibraltar Defence Police">Gibraltar Defence Police</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RGP_Patrol_Car.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/RGP_Patrol_Car.JPG/220px-RGP_Patrol_Car.JPG" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/RGP_Patrol_Car.JPG/330px-RGP_Patrol_Car.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/RGP_Patrol_Car.JPG/440px-RGP_Patrol_Car.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1156" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RGP_Patrol_Car.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Royal Gibraltar Police car, 2012</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:K20P1600.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/K20P1600.JPG/220px-K20P1600.JPG" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/K20P1600.JPG/330px-K20P1600.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/K20P1600.JPG/440px-K20P1600.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4672" data-file-height="3104" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:K20P1600.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Royal_Gibraltar_Police" title="Royal Gibraltar Police">Royal Gibraltar Police</a>, Marine Section</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Gibraltar_Police" title="Royal Gibraltar Police">Royal Gibraltar Police</a> (RGP), <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Defence_Police" title="Gibraltar Defence Police">Gibraltar Defence Police</a> (GDP) and <a href="/wiki/Her_Majesty%27s_Customs_(Gibraltar)" title="Her Majesty&#39;s Customs (Gibraltar)">Her Majesty\'s Customs (Gibraltar)</a> are Gibraltar\'s principal civilian <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_agency" title="Law enforcement agency">law enforcement agencies</a>. Outside the United Kingdom, the RGP is the oldest police force of the former <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a>, formed shortly after the creation of London\'s <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Police" class="mw-redirect" title="Metropolitan Police">Metropolitan Police</a> in 1829 when Gibraltar was declared a <a href="/wiki/Crown_colony" title="Crown colony">crown colony</a> on 25 June 1830.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In general, the Gibraltar force follows British police models in its dress and its mostly male constables and sergeants on foot patrol wear the traditional <a href="/wiki/Custodian_helmet" title="Custodian helmet">custodian helmet</a>, the headgear of the British "bobby on the beat". The helmet is traditionally made of cork covered outside by felt or <a href="/wiki/Serge_(fabric)" title="Serge (fabric)">serge</a>-like material that matches the tunic. The vehicles also appear virtually identical to typical UK police vehicles, but are <a href="/wiki/Left_hand_drive" class="mw-redirect" title="Left hand drive">left hand drive</a>.\n</p><p>The force, whose name received the prefix "Royal" in 1992, currently numbers over 220 officers divided into a number of units. These include the <a href="/wiki/Criminal_Investigation_Department" class="mw-redirect" title="Criminal Investigation Department">CID</a>, drug squad, <a href="/wiki/Special_branch" class="mw-redirect" title="Special branch">special branch</a>, firearms, <a href="/wiki/Scenes_of_Crime_Officer" class="mw-redirect" title="Scenes of Crime Officer">scene of crime examiners</a>, traffic, marine and operations units, sections or departments.\n</p><p>On 24 September 2015, the Freedom of the City of Gibraltar was conferred upon the RGP by the Mayor, Adolfo Canepa.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Armed_forces">Armed forces</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gibraltar&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Armed forces">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Gibraltar\'s defence is the responsibility of the United Kingdom tri-services <a href="/wiki/British_Forces_Gibraltar" title="British Forces Gibraltar">British Forces Gibraltar</a>. In January 2007, the Ministry of Defence announced that the private company <a href="/wiki/Serco" title="Serco">Serco</a> would provide services to the base. The announcement resulted in the affected trade unions striking.\n</p>\n<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Gibraltar_Regiment" title="Royal Gibraltar Regiment">Royal Gibraltar Regiment</a> provides the army garrison with a detachment of the <a href="/wiki/British_Army" title="British Army">British Army</a>, based at <i>Devils Tower Camp</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> The regiment was originally a part-time reserve force until the British Army placed it on a permanent footing in 1990. The regiment includes full-time and part-time soldiers recruited from Gibraltar as well as British Army regulars posted from other regiments.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> maintains a <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar_Squadron" title="Gibraltar Squadron">squadron</a> at the Rock. The squadron is responsible for the security and integrity of British Gibraltar Territorial Waters (BGTW). The shore establishment at Gibraltar is called <a href="/wiki/HMS_Rooke" title="HMS Rooke">HMS <i>Rooke</i></a> after <a href="/wiki/Sir_George_Rooke" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir George Rooke">Sir George Rooke</a>, who captured the Rock for <a href="/wiki/Charles_VI,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles VI, Holy Roman Emperor">Archduke Charles</a> (pretender to the Spanish throne) in 1704. The naval air base was named HMS <i>Cormorant.</i> Gibraltar\'s strategic position provides an important facility for the Royal Navy and Britain\'s allies. British and US nuclear submarines frequently visit the <i>Z berths</i> at Gibraltar.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Berth_(moorings)" title="Berth (moorings)">Z berth</a> provides the facility for nuclear submarines to visit for operational or recreational purposes and for non-nuclear repairs. During the <a href="/wiki/Falklands_War" title="Falklands War">Falklands War</a>, an Argentine plan to attack British shipping in the harbour using frogmen (<a href="/wiki/Operation_Algeciras" title="Operation Algeciras">Operation Algeciras</a>) was foiled.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> The naval base also played a part in supporting the task force sent by Britain to recover the Falklands.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a> station at Gibraltar forms part of Headquarters British Forces Gibraltar. Although aircraft are no longer permanently stationed at <a href="/wiki/RAF_Gibraltar" title="RAF Gibraltar">RAF Gibraltar</a>, a variety of RAF aircraft make regular visits and the airfield also houses a section from the <a href="/wiki/Met_Office" title="Met Office">Met Office</a>.</li></ul>\n<p>Gibraltar has an important role in <a href="/wiki/Signals_intelligence" title="Signals intelligence">UKSIGINT</a> and provides a vital strategic part of the United Kingdom communications gathering and monitoring network in the Mediterranean and North Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">\n\t\t<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 185px"><div style="width: 185px">\n\t\t\t<div class="thumb" style="width: 180px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a class="gallerytext">\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a>\'s base in Gibraltar.\n</p>\n\t\t\t</div>\n\t\t</div></li>\n</ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline"
